```
TITLE: Angular HttpClient PUT Method Overloads
DESCRIPTION: Details the various overloads for the HttpClient 'put' method, allowing for different response types and generic type parameters. It covers configurations for headers, parameters, progress reporting, and credentials.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/goldens/public-api/common/http/index.api.md#_snippet_24

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
HttpClient PUT Method:

This method sends a PUT request to the specified URL. It supports multiple overloads to handle different response types and generic return types.

Overloads:

1.  `put(url: string, body: any | null, options: { observe: 'response', responseType: 'arraybuffer', ... }): Observable<HttpResponse<ArrayBuffer>>`
    - Sends a PUT request and expects the response body as an ArrayBuffer.
    - Parameters:
        - `url`: The URL to send the request to.
        - `body`: The request body.
        - `options`: Configuration object including `observe`, `responseType`, `headers`, `params`, `reportProgress`, `withCredentials`, `timeout`, etc.
    - Returns: An Observable emitting an `HttpResponse` with an `ArrayBuffer` body.

2.  `put(url: string, body: any | null, options: { observe: 'response', responseType: 'blob', ... }): Observable<HttpResponse<Blob>>`
    - Sends a PUT request and expects the response body as a Blob.
    - Parameters:
        - `url`: The URL to send the request to.
        - `body`: The request body.
        - `options`: Configuration object including `observe`, `responseType`, `headers`, `params`, `reportProgress`, `withCredentials`, `timeout`, etc.
    - Returns: An Observable emitting an `HttpResponse` with a `Blob` body.

3.  `put(url: string, body: any | null, options: { observe: 'response', responseType: 'text', ... }): Observable<HttpResponse<string>>`
    - Sends a PUT request and expects the response body as plain text.
    - Parameters:
        - `url`: The URL to send the request to.
        - `body`: The request body.
        - `options`: Configuration object including `observe`, `responseType`, `headers`, `params`, `reportProgress`, `withCredentials`, `timeout`, etc.
    - Returns: An Observable emitting an `HttpResponse` with a `string` body.

4.  `put(url: string, body: any | null, options: { observe: 'response', responseType?: 'json', ... }): Observable<HttpResponse<Object>>`
    - Sends a PUT request and expects the response body as a JSON object (default behavior).
    - Parameters:
        - `url`: The URL to send the request to.
        - `body`: The request body.
        - `options`: Configuration object including `observe`, `responseType`, `headers`, `params`, `reportProgress`, `withCredentials`, `timeout`, etc.
    - Returns: An Observable emitting an `HttpResponse` with an `Object` body.

5.  `put<T>(url: string, body: any | null, options: { observe: 'response', responseType?: 'json', ... }): Observable<HttpResponse<T>>`
    - Sends a PUT request and expects the response body as a JSON object, with a generic type `T` for the response.
    - Parameters:
        - `url`: The URL to send the request to.
        - `body`: The request body.
        - `options`: Configuration object including `observe`, `responseType`, `headers`, `params`, `reportProgress`, `withCredentials`, `timeout`, etc.
    - Returns: An Observable emitting an `HttpResponse` with a body of type `T`.

6.  `put(url: string, body: any | null, options?: { observe: 'body', responseType?: 'json', ... }): Observable<Object>`
    - Sends a PUT request and returns only the response body as a JSON object.
    - Parameters:
        - `url`: The URL to send the request to.
        - `body`: The request body.
        - `options`: Configuration object including `observe`, `responseType`, `headers`, `params`, `reportProgress`, `withCredentials`, `timeout`, etc.
    - Returns: An Observable emitting the response body as an `Object`.

7.  `put<T>(url: string, body: any | null, options?: { observe: 'body', responseType?: 'json', ... }): Observable<T>`
    - Sends a PUT request and returns only the response body with a generic type `T`.
    - Parameters:
        - `url`: The URL to send the request to.
        - `body`: The request body.
        - `options`: Configuration object including `observe`, `responseType`, `headers`, `params`, `reportProgress`, `withCredentials`, `timeout`, etc.
    - Returns: An Observable emitting the response body of type `T`.

Common Options:
- `headers`: `HttpHeaders | Record<string, string | string[]>` - Sets request headers.
- `context`: `HttpContext` - Sets context for the request.
- `params`: `HttpParams | Record<string, string | number | boolean | ReadonlyArray<string | number | boolean>>` - Sets URL query parameters.
- `reportProgress`: `boolean` - Enables reporting of progress events.
- `withCredentials`: `boolean` - Indicates whether to include credentials.
- `credentials`: `RequestCredentials` - Specifies credentials for cross-origin requests.
- `keepalive`: `boolean` - Keeps the connection alive.
- `priority`: `RequestPriority` - Sets the request priority.
- `cache`: `RequestCache` - Configures caching behavior.
- `mode`: `RequestMode` - Sets the mode for the request (e.g., 'cors', 'no-cors').
- `redirect`: `RequestRedirect` - Sets the redirect mode.
- `referrer`: `string` - Specifies the referrer.
- `integrity`: `string` - Provides the Subresource Integrity value.
- `timeout`: `number` - Sets a timeout for the request in milliseconds.
```

TITLE: URL Handling Methods
DESCRIPTION: Provides methods for encoding search parameters, normalizing URLs, and parsing URL strings. These methods are crucial for managing and manipulating URLs within Angular applications.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/goldens/public-api/common/upgrade/index.api.md#_snippet_6

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
URL Handling Methods:

encodeSearch(search: string | { [k: string]: unknown; }): string
  - Encodes search parameters into a URL-friendly string.
  - Parameters:
    - search: A string representing search parameters or an object containing key-value pairs for search parameters.
  - Returns: A string representing the encoded search parameters.

normalize(href: string): string
normalize(path: string, search: { [k: string]: unknown; }, hash: string, baseUrl?: string): string
  - Normalizes a given URL or path. This method handles different input formats and ensures consistency.
  - Overloaded signatures:
    - normalize(href: string): Normalizes a full URL string.
    - normalize(path: string, search: { [k: string]: unknown; }, hash: string, baseUrl?: string): Normalizes a path with optional search parameters, hash, and base URL.
  - Parameters:
    - href: The URL string to normalize.
    - path: The path string to normalize.
    - search: An object containing search parameters.
    - hash: The hash fragment of the URL.
    - baseUrl: An optional base URL to resolve relative paths.
  - Returns: The normalized URL string.

parse(url: string, base?: string): { href: string; protocol: string; host: string; search: string; hash: string; hostname: string; port: string; pathname: string; }
  - Parses a URL string into its constituent parts.
  - Parameters:
    - url: The URL string to parse.
    - base: An optional base URL to resolve relative URLs.
  - Returns: An object containing the parsed URL components: href, protocol, host, search, hash, hostname, port, and pathname.
```

TITLE: Angular EXPANDO: Component, Directive, and Host Binding Example
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates the Angular `EXPANDO` concept for data size unknown at compile time. This example shows a parent component (`MyApp`), a child component (`Child`), and a directive (`Tooltip`), highlighting the use of `@HostBinding`. The code utilizes Angular's internal compilation decorators like `ɵɵdefineComponent` and `ɵɵdefineDirective` to illustrate these concepts.
```

})

  static ɵcmp = ɵɵdefineComponent({
    ...,
    decls: 1,
    template: function(rf: RenderFlags, ctx: MyApp) {
      if (rf & RenderFlags.Create) {
        ɵɵelement(0, 'child', ['tooltip', null]);
      }
      ...
    },
    directives: [Child, Tooltip]
  });
}


@Component({
  selector: 'child',
  ...
})
class Child {
  @HostBinding('tooltip') hostTitle = 'Hello World!';
  static ɵcmp = ɵɵdefineComponent({
    ...
    hostVars: 1
  });
  ...
}

@Directive({
  selector: '[tooltip]'
})
class Tooltip {
  @HostBinding('title') hostTitle = 'greeting';
  static ɵdir = ɵɵdefineDirective({
    ...
    hostVars: 1
  });
  ...
}

import { inject, viewChildren, afterNextRender } from '@angular/core';
import { AnimationCreatorService, AnimationLayerDirective } from '...'; // Assuming correct import path

  private animationCreator = inject(AnimationCreatorService);
  layers = viewChildren(AnimationLayerDirective);

  constructor() {

      // The layers must be provided

    }});

```
TITLE: Angular Component Input Examples and Narrowing
DESCRIPTION: Comprehensive examples of Angular component inputs, including required inputs with transformations, type narrowing, and control flow usage. Demonstrates handling different input types and conditional logic.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/packages/core/schematics/migrations/signal-migration/test/golden.txt#_snippet_22

LANGUAGE: TypeScript
CODE:
```
// tslint:disable

import {Component, Input, input} from '@angular/core';

interface Vehicle {}
interface Car extends Vehicle {
  __car: true;
}
interface Audi extends Car {
  __audi: true;
}

// Dummy transform function for demonstration
function disabledTransform(value: string | boolean): boolean {
  return value === 'true' || value === true;
}

// Dummy type guard functions for demonstration
function isCar(v: Vehicle | null): v is Car {
  return !!v && '__car' in v;
}
function isAudi(v: Car | null): v is Audi {
  return !!v && '__audi' in v;
}

@Component({
  selector: 'app-component',
  templateUrl: './template.html',
})
export class AppComponent {
  readonly input = input<string | null>(null);
  readonly bla = input.required<boolean, string | boolean>({ transform: disabledTransform });
  readonly narrowableMultipleTimes = input<Vehicle | null>(null);
  readonly withUndefinedInput = input<string>();
  // TODO: Skipped for migration because:
  //  Your application code writes to the input. This prevents migration.
  @Input() incompatible: string | null = null;

  private _bla: any;
  // TODO: Skipped for migration because:
  //  Accessor inputs cannot be migrated as they are too complex.
  @Input()
  set ngSwitch(newValue: any) {
    this._bla = newValue;
    if (newValue === 0) {
      console.log('test');
    }
  }

  someControlFlowCase() {
    const input = this.input();
    if (input) {
      input.charAt(0);
    }
  }

  moreComplexControlFlowCase() {
    const input = this.input();
    if (!input) {
      return;
    }

    this.doSomething();

    (() => {
      // might be a different input value now?! 
      // No! it can't because we don't allow writes to ""input""!!.
      console.log(input.substring(0));
    })();
  }

  doSomething() {
    this.incompatible = 'some other value';
  }

  vsd() {
    const input = this.input();
    const narrowableMultipleTimes = this.narrowableMultipleTimes();
    if (!input && narrowableMultipleTimes !== null) {
      return narrowableMultipleTimes;
    }
    return input ? 'eager' : 'lazy';
  }

  allTheSameNoNarrowing() {
    const input = this.input();
    console.log(input);
    console.log(input);
  }

  test() {
    if (this.narrowableMultipleTimes()) {
      console.log();

      const x = () => {
        // @ts-expect-error
        if (isCar(this.narrowableMultipleTimes())) {
        }
      };

      console.log();
      console.log();
      x();
      x();
    }
  }

  extremeNarrowingNested() {
    const narrowableMultipleTimes = this.narrowableMultipleTimes();
    if (narrowableMultipleTimes && isCar(narrowableMultipleTimes)) {
      narrowableMultipleTimes.__car;

      let car = narrowableMultipleTimes;
      let ctx = this;

      function nestedFn() {
        if (isAudi(car)) {
          console.log(car.__audi);
        }
      }
    }
  }
}
```

TITLE: Angular Hydration Mismatch: Direct DOM Manipulation
DESCRIPTION: This TypeScript example demonstrates how directly manipulating the DOM using native browser APIs, such as `insertBefore` with a newly created element, can lead to an Angular hydration node mismatch error. The error occurs because Angular's client-side hydration process expects the DOM structure to match what was server-rendered, and unexpected DOM changes break this expectation.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/adev/src/content/reference/errors/NG0500.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
@Component({
  selector: 'app-example',
  template: '<div><span>world</span></div>',
})
export class ExampleComponent {
  hostElement = inject(ElementRef).nativeElement;

  ngOnInit() {
    // Create a new <p> element with the `Hello` text inside
    const newNode = document.createElement('p');
    newNode.innerHTML = 'Hello';

    // Insert the <p> before the first element. Since Angular has no information
   // about the <p> element, it will be looking for the <div> element at the first
   // element position instead. As a result, a hydration mismatch error would be
   // thrown. Instead, update component's template to create the <p> element.
   this.hostElement.insertBefore(newNode, this.hostElement.firstChild);
 }
}
```

TITLE: Pull Request Target Scenarios
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates common scenarios for pull requests, mapping desired actions to the appropriate target branch and label, and explaining where the change will ultimately land.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/contributing-docs/branches-and-versioning.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: markdown
CODE:
```
| I want to...                                                | Target branch           | Target label | Your change will land in...                                                                                                |
|-----------------------------------------------------------|-----------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Make a non-breaking bug fix                                 | `main`                  | `patch`      | `main`, the active patch branch, and the active RC branch if there is one                                                  |
| Introduce a new feature                                     | `main`                  | `minor`      | `main` (any time)                                                                                                          |
| Make a breaking change                                      | `main`                  | `major`      | `main` (only when `main` represents the next major version)                                                                |
| Make a critical security fix                                | `main`                  | `lts`        | `main`, the active patch branch, the active RC branch if there is one, and all branches for versions within the LTS window |
| Bump the version of an RC                                   | the active RC branch    | `rc`         | The active RC branch                                                                                                       |
| Fix an RC bug for a major release feature                   | `main`                  | `rc`         | `main` and the active RC branch                                                                                            |
| Backport a bug fix to the `latest` npm version during an RC | the active patch branch | `patch`      | the active patch branch only                                                                                               |
```

TITLE: MyPopupHarness Example
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates a component harness for a popup component (`MyPopupHarness`). It shows how to define selectors for internal elements (`getTriggerElement`, `getContentElement`) and implement methods (`toggle`, `isOpen`) for interacting with the popup's state and trigger.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/adev/src/content/guide/testing/creating-component-harnesses.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
class MyPopupHarness extends ComponentHarness {
  static hostSelector = 'my-popup';

  protected getTriggerElement = this.locatorFor('button');
  protected getContentElement = this.locatorForOptional('.my-popup-content');

  /** Toggles the open state of the popup. */
  async toggle() {
    const trigger = await this.getTriggerElement();
    return trigger.click();
  }

  /** Checks if the popup us open. */
  async isOpen() {
    const content = await this.getContentElement();
    return !!content;
  }
}
```

TITLE: Benchpress Benchmark Driver Example
DESCRIPTION: This JavaScript code demonstrates how to write a benchmark driver using Benchpress. It shows how to initialize a runner, navigate to the application, find elements, and execute a benchmark sample with preparation and execution steps.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/packages/benchpress/README.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
// A runner contains the shared configuration
// and can be shared across multiple tests.
var runner = new Runner(...);

driver.get('http://myserver/index.html');

var resetBtn = driver.findElement(By.id('reset'));
var fillBtn = driver.findElement(By.id('fill'));

runner.sample({
  id: 'fillElement',
  // Prepare is optional...
  prepare: () {
    resetBtn.click();
  },
  execute: () {
    fillBtn.click();
    // Note: if fillBtn would use some asynchronous code,
    // we would need to wait here for its end.
  }
});
```

TITLE: Angular Catalyst Fake Async Testing with Input Signals
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates using Angular's Catalyst fake async testing utilities. Similar to the async example, it shows bootstrapping a template with component inputs and using `UnwrapSignalInputs` for type safety with signal inputs.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/packages/core/schematics/migrations/signal-migration/test/golden_best_effort.txt#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { UnwrapSignalInputs } from ""google3/javascript/angular2/testing/catalyst/fake_async"";
// tslint:disable

import {input} from '@angular/core';

// google3/javascript/angular2/testing/catalyst/fake_async
// ^^ this allows the advisor to even consider this file.

function it(msg: string, fn: () => void) {}
function bootstrapTemplate(tmpl: string, inputs: unknown) {}

class MyComp {
  readonly hello = input('');
}

it('should work', () => {
  const inputs = {
    hello: 'test',
  } as Partial<UnwrapSignalInputs<MyComp>>;
  bootstrapTemplate('<my-comp [hello]=""hello"">', inputs);
});
```

TITLE: HttpResourceRef Interface
DESCRIPTION: Represents a reference to an HTTP resource, providing access to its value, loading state, headers, and progress. Includes a destroy method for cleanup.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/goldens/public-api/common/http/index.api.md#_snippet_42

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
HttpResourceRef<T>:
  // Extends WritableResource and ResourceRef for resource management.
  // Method to clean up the resource and its subscriptions.
  destroy(): void;
  // Type guard to check if the resource currently holds a defined value.
  hasValue(): this is HttpResourceRef<Exclude<T, undefined>>;
  // Signal containing the HTTP headers of the response.
  readonly headers: Signal<HttpHeaders | undefined>;
  // Signal containing the HTTP progress event during the request.
  readonly progress: Signal<HttpProgressEvent | undefined>;
  // Signal containing the HTTP status code of the response.
  readonly statusCode: Signal<number | undefined>;

```

TITLE: Angular Resource API for Streaming Data Updates
DESCRIPTION: Implements a client-side streaming pattern using Angular's `resource` API. The `stream` property accepts an asynchronous function that updates a signal value over time as data chunks are received from a fetch request. It handles decoding chunks and updating the signal with either new data or errors.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/adev/src/content/ai/overview.md#_snippet_10

LANGUAGE: ts
CODE:
```
characters = resource({
    stream: async () => {
      const data = signal<{ value: string } | { error: unknown }>({ value: """" });

      fetch(this.url).then(async (response) => {
        if (!response.body) return;
        
        for await (const chunk of response.body) {
          const chunkText = this.decoder.decode(chunk);
          data.update((prev) => {
            if (""value"" in prev) {
              return { value: `${prev.value} ${chunkText}` };
            } else {
              return { error: chunkText };
            }
          });
        }
      });

      return data;
    },
  });

  // Renders the defer block in a specified state.
  render(state: DeferBlockState): Promise<void>;
  // Retrieves defer block fixtures nested within this block.
  getDeferBlocks(): Promise<DeferBlockFixture[]>;

  // Enum for defer block rendering states.
  // DeferBlockState:
  //   Placeholder = 0,

```
TITLE: Angular HTTP Client Configuration
DESCRIPTION: Provides functions to configure Angular's HttpClient. These functions are used with `provideHttpClient` to customize features like fetch support, interceptors, JSONP, and XSRF protection.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/goldens/public-api/common/http/index.api.md#_snippet_51

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
provideHttpClient(...features: HttpFeature<HttpFeatureKind>[]): EnvironmentProviders
  - Configures the HttpClient for the application. Accepts various feature functions to customize its behavior.
  - Parameters:
    - features: An array of HttpFeature configurations.
  - Returns: EnvironmentProviders - Providers to be added to the Angular environment.

withFetch(): HttpFeature<HttpFeatureKind.Fetch>
  - Enables the use of the browser's native `fetch` API for making HTTP requests.
  - Returns: HttpFeature - A feature configuration object.

withInterceptors(interceptorFns: HttpInterceptorFn[]): HttpFeature<HttpFeatureKind.Interceptors>
  - Configures custom interceptors to be applied to HTTP requests.
  - Parameters:
    - interceptorFns: An array of HttpInterceptorFn functions.
  - Returns: HttpFeature - A feature configuration object.

withInterceptorsFromDi(): HttpFeature<HttpFeatureKind.LegacyInterceptors>
  - Enables interceptors that are provided via dependency injection (DI).
  - Returns: HttpFeature - A feature configuration object.

withJsonpSupport(): HttpFeature<HttpFeatureKind.JsonpSupport>
  - Enables JSONP support for making cross-origin JSON requests.
  - Returns: HttpFeature - A feature configuration object.

withNoXsrfProtection(): HttpFeature<HttpFeatureKind.NoXsrfProtection>
  - Disables the default XSRF protection mechanism.
  - Returns: HttpFeature - A feature configuration object.

withRequestsMadeViaParent(): HttpFeature<HttpFeatureKind.RequestsMadeViaParent>
  - Configures requests to be made via the parent injector context.
  - Returns: HttpFeature - A feature configuration object.

withXsrfConfiguration({ cookieName, headerName, }: { cookieName?: string; headerName?: string; }): HttpFeature<HttpKind.CustomXsrfConfiguration>
  - Configures custom cookie and header names for XSRF protection.
  - Parameters:
    - cookieName: The name of the XSRF cookie (optional).
    - headerName: The name of the XSRF header (optional).
  - Returns: HttpFeature - A feature configuration object.
```

TITLE: HttpClient POST Method Overloads
DESCRIPTION: This entry details the multiple overloads for the `post` method of Angular's `HttpClient`. It specifies how to make POST requests with different response types (ArrayBuffer, Blob, text, JSON) and observation strategies ('events' or 'response'). Each overload includes common options like headers, context, parameters, and request-specific configurations such as cache, timeout, and credentials.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/goldens/public-api/common/http/index.api.md#_snippet_20

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
HttpClient.post

Makes a POST request to the given URL.

Overloads:

1.  post(url: string, body: any | null, options: {
        headers?: HttpHeaders | Record<string, string | string[]>;
        observe: 'events';
        context?: HttpContext;
        params?: HttpParams | Record<string, string | number | boolean | ReadonlyArray<string | number | boolean>>;
        reportProgress?: boolean;
        responseType: 'arraybuffer';
        withCredentials?: boolean;
        credentials?: RequestCredentials;
        keepalive?: boolean;
        priority?: RequestPriority;
        cache?: RequestCache;
        mode?: RequestMode;
        redirect?: RequestRedirect;
        referrer?: string;
        integrity?: string;
        transferCache?: {
            includeHeaders?: string[];
        } | boolean;
        timeout?: number;
    }): Observable<HttpEvent<ArrayBuffer>>;
    - Description: Sends a POST request and returns an observable of `HttpEvent` for `ArrayBuffer` responses, including progress events.
    - Parameters:
        - url: The URL to send the request to.
        - body: The request body.
        - options: Configuration options for the request.
            - observe: Must be 'events' to receive progress events.
            - responseType: Must be 'arraybuffer' for binary data.
    - Returns: An `Observable` emitting `HttpEvent` objects.

2.  post(url: string, body: any | null, options: {
        headers?: HttpHeaders | Record<string, string | string[]>;
        observe: 'events';
        context?: HttpContext;
        params?: HttpParams | Record<string, string | number | boolean | ReadonlyArray<string | number | boolean>>;
        reportProgress?: boolean;
        responseType: 'blob';
        withCredentials?: boolean;
        credentials?: RequestCredentials;
        keepalive?: boolean;
        priority?: RequestPriority;
        cache?: RequestCache;
        mode?: RequestMode;
        redirect?: RequestRedirect;
        referrer?: string;
        integrity?: string;
        transferCache?: {
            includeHeaders?: string[];
        } | boolean;
        timeout?: number;
    }): Observable<HttpEvent<Blob>>;
    - Description: Sends a POST request and returns an observable of `HttpEvent` for `Blob` responses, including progress events.
    - Parameters:
        - url: The URL to send the request to.
        - body: The request body.
        - options: Configuration options for the request.
            - observe: Must be 'events' to receive progress events.
            - responseType: Must be 'blob' for binary data like files.
    - Returns: An `Observable` emitting `HttpEvent` objects.

3.  post(url: string, body: any | null, options: {
        headers?: HttpHeaders | Record<string, string | string[]>;
        observe: 'events';
        context?: HttpContext;
        params?: HttpParams | Record<string, string | number | boolean | ReadonlyArray<string | number | boolean>>;
        reportProgress?: boolean;
        responseType: 'text';
        withCredentials?: boolean;
        credentials?: RequestCredentials;
        keepalive?: boolean;
        priority?: RequestPriority;
        cache?: RequestCache;
        mode?: RequestMode;
        redirect?: RequestRedirect;
        referrer?: string;
        integrity?: string;
        transferCache?: {
            includeHeaders?: string[];
        } | boolean;
        timeout?: number;
    }): Observable<HttpEvent<string>>;
    - Description: Sends a POST request and returns an observable of `HttpEvent` for `string` responses, including progress events.
    - Parameters:
        - url: The URL to send the request to.
        - body: The request body.
        - options: Configuration options for the request.
            - observe: Must be 'events' to receive progress events.
            - responseType: Must be 'text' for plain text responses.
    - Returns: An `Observable` emitting `HttpEvent` objects.

4.  post(url: string, body: any | null, options: {
        headers?: HttpHeaders | Record<string, string | string[]>;
        observe: 'events';
        context?: HttpContext;
        params?: HttpParams | Record<string, string | number | boolean | ReadonlyArray<string | number | boolean>>;
        reportProgress?: boolean;
        responseType?: 'json';
        withCredentials?: boolean;
        credentials?: RequestCredentials;
        keepalive?: boolean;
        priority?: RequestPriority;
        cache?: RequestCache;
        mode?: RequestMode;
        redirect?: RequestRedirect;
        referrer?: string;
        integrity?: string;
        transferCache?: {
            includeHeaders?: string[];
        } | boolean;
        timeout?: number;
    }): Observable<HttpEvent<Object>>;
    - Description: Sends a POST request and returns an observable of `HttpEvent` for `Object` responses (default JSON parsing), including progress events.
    - Parameters:
        - url: The URL to send the request to.
        - body: The request body.
        - options: Configuration options for the request.
            - observe: Must be 'events' to receive progress events.
            - responseType: Defaults to 'json' if not specified.
    - Returns: An `Observable` emitting `HttpEvent` objects.

5.  post<T>(url: string, body: any | null, options: {
        headers?: HttpHeaders | Record<string, string | string[]>;
        observe: 'events';
        context?: HttpContext;
        params?: HttpParams | Record<string, string | number | boolean | ReadonlyArray<string | number | boolean>>;
        reportProgress?: boolean;
        responseType?: 'json';
        withCredentials?: boolean;
        credentials?: RequestCredentials;
        keepalive?: boolean;
        priority?: RequestPriority;
        cache?: RequestCache;
        mode?: RequestMode;
        redirect?: RequestRedirect;
        referrer?: string;
        integrity?: string;
        transferCache?: {
            includeHeaders?: string[];
        } | boolean;
        timeout?: number;
    }): Observable<HttpEvent<T>>;
    - Description: Sends a POST request and returns an observable of `HttpEvent` for typed JSON responses, including progress events.
    - Parameters:
        - url: The URL to send the request to.
        - body: The request body.
        - options: Configuration options for the request.
            - observe: Must be 'events' to receive progress events.
            - responseType: Defaults to 'json' if not specified.
    - Returns: An `Observable` emitting `HttpEvent` objects of type `T`.

6.  post(url: string, body: any | null, options: {
        headers?: HttpHeaders | Record<string, string | string[]>;
        observe: 'response';
        context?: HttpContext;
        params?: HttpParams | Record<string, string | number | boolean | ReadonlyArray<string | number | boolean>>;
        reportProgress?: boolean;
        responseType: 'arraybuffer';
        withCredentials?: boolean;
        credentials?: RequestCredentials;
        keepalive?: boolean;
        priority?: RequestPriority;
        cache?: RequestCache;
        mode?: RequestMode;
        redirect?: RequestRedirect;
        referrer?: string;
        integrity?: string;
        transferCache?: {
            includeHeaders?: string[];
        } | boolean;
        timeout?: number;
    }): Observable<HttpResponse<ArrayBuffer>>;
    - Description: Sends a POST request and returns an observable of the full `HttpResponse` for `ArrayBuffer` responses.
    - Parameters:
        - url: The URL to send the request to.
        - body: The request body.
        - options: Configuration options for the request.
            - observe: Must be 'response' to receive the full `HttpResponse`.
            - responseType: Must be 'arraybuffer' for binary data.
    - Returns: An `Observable` emitting `HttpResponse` objects.

7.  post(url: string, body: any | null, options: {
        headers?: HttpHeaders | Record<string, string | string[]>;
        observe: 'response';
        context?: HttpContext;
        params?: HttpParams | Record<string, string | number | boolean | ReadonlyArray<string | number | boolean>>;
        reportProgress?: boolean;
        responseType: 'blob';
        withCredentials?: boolean;
        credentials?: RequestCredentials;
        keepalive?: boolean;
        priority?: RequestPriority;
        cache?: RequestCache;
        mode?: RequestMode;
        redirect?: RequestRedirect;
        referrer?: string;
        integrity?: string;
        transferCache?: {
            includeHeaders?: string[];
        } | boolean;
        timeout?: number;
    }): Observable<HttpResponse<Blob>>;
    - Description: Sends a POST request and returns an observable of the full `HttpResponse` for `Blob` responses.
    - Parameters:
        - url: The URL to send the request to.
        - body: The request body.
        - options: Configuration options for the request.
            - observe: Must be 'response' to receive the full `HttpResponse`.
            - responseType: Must be 'blob' for binary data like files.
    - Returns: An `Observable` emitting `HttpResponse` objects.

Common Options:
    - headers: HTTP headers to send with the request.
    - context: HTTP context for the request.
    - params: URL parameters for the request.
    - reportProgress: Whether to report upload/download progress.
    - withCredentials: Whether to send credentials.
    - credentials: Custom credentials.
    - keepalive: Whether to keep the connection alive.
    - priority: Request priority.
    - cache: Request caching configuration.
    - mode: Request mode (e.g., 'cors').
    - redirect: Redirect behavior.
    - referrer: Referrer information.
    - integrity: Subresource Integrity value.
    - transferCache: Configuration for transfer cache.
    - timeout: Request timeout in milliseconds.
```

TITLE: Angular Resource Management
DESCRIPTION: Defines interfaces and types for managing asynchronous data resources, including loading states, error handling, and streaming capabilities.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/goldens/public-api/core/index.api.md#_snippet_83

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Resource<T>
  - Represents a resource with loading, error, and value states.
  - Properties:
    - error: Signal<Error | undefined> - The error if the resource failed to load.
    - isLoading: Signal<boolean> - Indicates if the resource is currently loading.
    - status: Signal<ResourceStatus> - The current status of the resource.
    - value: Signal<T> - The loaded value of the resource.
  - Methods:
    - hasValue(): this is Resource<Exclude<T, undefined>> - Checks if the resource has a defined value.

ResourceLoader<T, R>
  - Type for a function that loads a resource asynchronously.
  - Signature: (param: ResourceLoaderParams<R>) => PromiseLike<T>

ResourceLoaderParams<R>
  - Parameters for a resource loader.
  - Properties:
    - abortSignal: AbortSignal - An AbortSignal for cancelling the operation.
    - params: NoInfer<Exclude<R, undefined>> - Parameters for the loader.
    - previous: { status: ResourceStatus } - The status of the previous resource load.

ResourceOptions<T, R>
  - Union type for resource loading options, either PromiseResourceOptions or StreamingResourceOptions.

ResourceRef<T>
  - Extends WritableResource<T> and provides methods to manage a resource.
  - Methods:
    - destroy(): void - Cleans up the resource.
    - hasValue(): this is ResourceRef<Exclude<T, undefined>> - Checks if the resource has a defined value.

ResourceStatus
  - Enum representing the possible states of a resource.
  - Values: 'idle' | 'error' | 'loading' | 'reloading' | 'resolved' | 'local'

ResourceStreamingLoader<T, R>
  - Type for a function that loads a resource and streams its updates.
  - Signature: (param: ResourceLoaderParams<R>) => PromiseLike<Signal<ResourceStreamItem<T>>>

ResourceStreamItem<T>
  - Represents an item in a resource stream, either a value or an error.
  - Types:
    - { value: T }
    - { error: Error }
```

TITLE: HeroDetailComponent Constructor and Parameter Handling
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates the constructor of the HeroDetailComponent, showing how it injects services like ActivatedRoute and HeroDetailService. It highlights the subscription to ActivatedRoute.paramMap to retrieve route parameters, specifically the hero ID, which is crucial for fetching component data.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/adev/src/content/guide/testing/components-scenarios.md#_snippet_38

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { Component, OnInit } from '@angular/core';
import { ActivatedRoute, ParamMap } from '@angular/router';
import { Location } from '@angular/common';
import { Hero } from '../hero';
import { HeroDetailService } from '../hero-detail.service';
import { Observable } from 'rxjs';
import { switchMap } from 'rxjs/operators';

@Component({
  selector: 'app-hero-detail',
  templateUrl: './hero-detail.component.html',
  styleUrls: ['./hero-detail.component.css']
})
export class HeroDetailComponent implements OnInit {
  hero$: Observable<Hero>;
  private sub: any; // Subscription

  constructor(
    private route: ActivatedRoute,
    private heroDetailService: HeroDetailService,
    private location: Location
  ) {}

  ngOnInit(): void {
    // Get hero details based on route parameter 'id'
    this.hero$ = this.route.paramMap.pipe(
      switchMap((params: ParamMap) => {
        // '+' converts string ID to number
        return this.heroDetailService.getHero(+params.get('id'));
      })
    );
  }

  // ... other methods like goBack, save ...
}


    credentials?: RequestCredentials;
    keepalive?: boolean;
    priority?: RequestPriority;
    cache?: RequestCache;
    mode?: RequestMode;
    redirect?: RequestRedirect;
    referrer?: string;
    integrity?: string;
    timeout?: number;
}): Observable<HttpResponse<string>>;

HttpClient.options(url: string, options: {
    headers?: HttpHeaders | Record<string, string | string[]>;
    observe: 'response';
    context?: HttpContext;
    params?: HttpParams | Record<string, string | number | boolean | ReadonlyArray<string | number | boolean>>;
    reportProgress?: boolean;
    responseType?: 'json';
    withCredentials?: boolean;
    credentials?: RequestCredentials;
    keepalive?: boolean;
    priority?: RequestPriority;
    cache?: RequestCache;
    mode?: RequestMode;
    redirect?: RequestRedirect;
    referrer?: string;
    integrity?: string;
    timeout?: number;
}): Observable<HttpResponse<Object>>;

HttpClient.options<T>(url: string, options: {
    headers?: HttpHeaders | Record<string, string | string[]>;
    observe: 'response';
    context?: HttpContext;
    params?: HttpParams | Record<string, string | number | boolean | ReadonlyArray<string | number | boolean>>;
    reportProgress?: boolean;
    responseType?: 'json';
    withCredentials?: boolean;
    credentials?: RequestCredentials;
    keepalive?: boolean;
    priority?: RequestPriority;
    cache?: RequestCache;
    mode?: RequestMode;
    redirect?: RequestRedirect;
    referrer?: string;
    integrity?: string;
    timeout?: number;
}): Observable<HttpResponse<T>>;

Parameters:
  url: string - The URL to which the request is sent.
  options: {
    headers?: HttpHeaders | Record<string, string | string[]> - Sets of HTTP headers to pass to the request or observable.
    observe: 'events' | 'body' | 'response' - Specifies how much of the response to return.
    context?: HttpContext - Set of HttpContext values for the request.
    params?: HttpParams | Record<string, string | number | boolean | ReadonlyArray<string | number | boolean>> - Sets of HTTP parameters to pass to the URL.
    reportProgress?: boolean - Whether to report progress events.
    responseType?: 'json' | 'text' | 'arraybuffer' | 'blob' - Specifies the type of the response body.
    withCredentials?: boolean - Whether to return credentials.
    credentials?: RequestCredentials - Credentials for the request.
    keepalive?: boolean - Whether to keep the connection alive.
    priority?: RequestPriority - Priority of the request.
    cache?: RequestCache - Cache configuration for the request.
    mode?: RequestMode - The mode for the request (e.g., 'cors', 'no-cors').
    redirect?: RequestRedirect - The redirect mode for the request.
    referrer?: string - The referrer for the request.
    integrity?: string - The integrity for the request.
    timeout?: number - The timeout for the request in milliseconds.
  }

Returns:
  Observable<HttpEvent<string>> | Observable<HttpEvent<Object>> | Observable<HttpEvent<T>> | Observable<HttpResponse<ArrayBuffer>> | Observable<HttpResponse<Blob>> | Observable<HttpResponse<string>> | Observable<HttpResponse<Object>> | Observable<HttpResponse<T>> - An observable of the HTTP event or response.

Related Methods:
  - HttpClient.request: A more general method for making HTTP requests.
  - HttpClient.get, HttpClient.post, HttpClient.put, HttpClient.delete, etc.: Specific HTTP method helpers.
```

TITLE: HttpClient POST with Progress Events
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to send data via POST request with HttpClient, enabling progress event reporting and observing the event stream. It handles upload progress and final response events.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/adev/src/content/guide/http/making-requests.md#_snippet_10

LANGUAGE: ts
CODE:
```
http.post('/api/upload', myData, {
  reportProgress: true,
  observe: 'events',
}).subscribe(event => {
  switch (event.type) {
    case HttpEventType.UploadProgress:
      console.log('Uploaded ' + event.loaded + ' out of ' + event.total + ' bytes');
      break;
    case HttpEventType.Response:
      console.log('Finished uploading!');
      break;
  }
});
```

TITLE: Builder Integration Test Example
DESCRIPTION: An example of an integration test for a custom builder using TypeScript. It sets up the Architect testing environment, runs the builder, and validates the output.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/adev/src/content/tools/cli/cli-builder.md#_snippet_15

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { Architect, BuilderOutput, BuilderRun } from '@angular-devkit/architect';
import { TestingArchitectHost } from '@angular-devkit/architect/testing';
import { join, normalize } from 'path';

// Mock the builder and its dependencies for testing
const mockBuilder = {
  run: (): Promise<BuilderOutput> => {
    // Simulate file copy operation
    return Promise.resolve({ success: true });
  }
};

describe('Copy File Builder', () => {
  let architect: Architect;
  let testArchitectHost: TestingArchitectHost;

  beforeEach(async () => {
    testArchitectHost = new TestingArchitectHost();
    // Register the mock builder
    testArchitectHost.registerBuilder('@example/copy-file:copy', mockBuilder as any);
    architect = new Architect(testArchitectHost);
  });

  it('should copy a file', async () => {
    const run = await architect.scheduleBuilder('copy-package', {
      source: 'package.json',
      destination: 'package-copy.json'
    });
    const output = await run.result;
    expect(output.success).toBe(true);
  });
});

```

TITLE: Route Reuse Strategy API
DESCRIPTION: Defines the interface for custom route reuse strategies. This allows control over which routes are detached, stored, retrieved, and reused during navigation.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/goldens/public-api/router/index.api.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
RouteReuseStrategy:
  retrieve(route: ActivatedRouteSnapshot): DetachedRouteHandle | null
    Called when the router needs to retrieve a detached route.
    Parameters:
      route: The route snapshot to retrieve.
    Returns:
      A detached route handle or null if no route is found.
  shouldAttach(route: ActivatedRouteSnapshot): boolean
    Called when the router needs to determine if a route should be attached.
    Parameters:
      route: The route snapshot to check.
    Returns:
      True if the route should be attached, false otherwise.
  shouldDetach(route: ActivatedRouteSnapshot): boolean
    Called when the router needs to determine if a route should be detached.
    Parameters:
      route: The route snapshot to check.
    Returns:
      True if the route should be detached, false otherwise.
  shouldReuseRoute(future: ActivatedRouteSnapshot, curr: ActivatedRouteSnapshot): boolean
    Called when the router needs to determine if two routes should be reused.
    Parameters:
      future: The future route snapshot.
      curr: The current route snapshot.
    Returns:
      True if the routes should be reused, false otherwise.
  store(route: ActivatedRouteSnapshot, detachedTree: DetachedRouteHandle): void
    Called when the router needs to store a detached route.
    Parameters:
      route: The route snapshot to store.
      detachedTree: The detached route handle to store.
```

TITLE: Optional Injection Before Non-Nullable Option
DESCRIPTION: This TypeScript example demonstrates a component with optional constructor-injected parameters, where one is implicitly non-nullable and the other explicitly nullable, before applying the `nonNullableOptional` migration option.
SOURCE: https://github.com/angular/angular/blob/main/adev/src/content/reference/migrations/inject-function.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { Component, Inject, Optional } from '@angular/core';
import { TOKEN_ONE, TOKEN_TWO } from './token';

@Component()
export class MyComp {
  constructor(
    @Inject(TOKEN_ONE) @Optional() private tokenOne: number,
    @Inject(TOKEN_TWO) @Optional() private tokenTwo: string | null) {}
}
